<div class="thumb tright"><div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg"><img class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2057" data-file-width="1354" decoding="async" height="334" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg/220px-Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg/330px-Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/e/e3/Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg/440px-Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a> <div class="thumbcaption"><div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Percentage_of_Australian_population_with_access_to_fluoridated_water_as_of_2012.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>Australian residents served with community water fluoridation, 2005<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157">[157]</a></sup> and 2012. The percentages are the proportions of the resident population served by public water supplies who are receiving fluoridated water.</div></div></div>
<link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1033289096" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><div class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Water_fluoridation_in_Australia" title="Water fluoridation in Australia">Water fluoridation in Australia</a></div>
<p>Australia now provides fluoridated water for 70% or more of the population in all states and territories. Many of Australia's drinking water supplies began fluoridation in the 1960s and 1970s. By 1984 almost 66% of the Australian population had access to fluoridated drinking water, represented by 850 towns and cities.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parliament_158-0"><a href="#cite_note-parliament-158">[158]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-commonwealth_159-0"><a href="#cite_note-commonwealth-159">[159]</a></sup> Some areas within Australia have <a href="/wiki/Fluoride#Occurrence" title="Fluoride">natural fluoride</a> levels in the groundwater, which was estimated in 1991 to provide drinking water to approximately 0.9% of the population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-parliament_158-1"><a href="#cite_note-parliament-158">[158]</a></sup>
</p><p>The first town to fluoridate the water supply in Australia was <a href="/wiki/Beaconsfield,_Tasmania" title="Beaconsfield, Tasmania">Beaconsfield, Tasmania</a> in 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-160"><a href="#cite_note-160">[160]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Queensland" title="Queensland">Queensland</a> became the last state to formally require the addition of fluoride to public drinking water supplies in December 2008.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-161"><a href="#cite_note-161">[161]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand">New Zealand</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_fluoridation_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=46" title="Edit section: New Zealand">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The use of water fluoridation first began in <a href="/wiki/Hastings,_New_Zealand" title="Hastings, New Zealand">Hastings, New Zealand</a> in 1954. A Commission of Inquiry was held in 1957 and then its use rapidly expanded in the mid 1960s.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-162"><a href="#cite_note-162">[162]</a></sup> New Zealand now has fluoridated water supplied to about half of the total population.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-163"><a href="#cite_note-163">[163]</a></sup> Of the six main centers, only <a href="/wiki/Christchurch" title="Christchurch">Christchurch</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-164"><a href="#cite_note-164">[164]</a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tauranga" title="Tauranga">Tauranga</a><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-165"><a href="#cite_note-165">[165]</a></sup> do not have a fluoridated water supply. <a href="/wiki/Wellington" title="Wellington">Wellington</a>'s water supply is mostly fluoridated, but the suburbs of <a href="/wiki/Petone" title="Petone">Petone</a> and <a href="/wiki/Korokoro,_New_Zealand" title="Korokoro, New Zealand">Korokoro</a> receive a non-fluoridated supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-166"><a href="#cite_note-166">[166]</a></sup> In <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a>, the suburbs <a href="/wiki/Onehunga" title="Onehunga">Onehunga</a> and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Huia_Village" title="Huia Village">Huia Village</a> don't fluoridate water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-167"><a href="#cite_note-167">[167]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2013, a <a href="/wiki/Hamilton,_New_Zealand" title="Hamilton, New Zealand">Hamilton</a> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Hamilton_City_Council" title="Hamilton City Council">City Council</a> committee voted to remove fluoride from late June 2013.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-168"><a href="#cite_note-168">[168]</a></sup> A referendum was held during the council elections in October 2013 with approximately 70% of voters voting for fluoride to be added back into the water supply, and in March 2014, the council voted 9 to 1 to re-introduce fluoride into the supply.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-169"><a href="#cite_note-169">[169]</a></sup> In a 2007 referendum about half of voters in the Central Otago, South Otago and the <a href="/wiki/Southland_Region" title="Southland Region">Southland Region</a> did not want fluoridation<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-170"><a href="#cite_note-170">[170]</a></sup> and voters in the <a href="/wiki/Waitaki_District" title="Waitaki District">Waitaki District</a> were against water fluoridation for all Wards.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-171"><a href="#cite_note-171">[171]</a></sup> Ashburton and Greymouth also voted against fluoridation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-172"><a href="#cite_note-172">[172]</a></sup>
</p><p>In 2014, the Prime Minister's Chief Science Advisor and the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Royal_Society_of_New_Zealand" title="Royal Society of New Zealand">Royal Society of New Zealand</a> published a report on the health effects of water fluoridation.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-173"><a href="#cite_note-173">[173]</a></sup>
</p><p>In June 2018, the <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_New_Zealand" title="Supreme Court of New Zealand">Supreme Court of New Zealand</a> in <i>New Health New Zealand Inc v South Taranaki District Council</i> upheld the legality of water fluoridation in New Zealand.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-174"><a href="#cite_note-174">[174]</a></sup>
</p><p>In late July 2022, Director-General of Health <a href="/wiki/Ashley_Bloomfield" title="Ashley Bloomfield">Ashley Bloomfield</a> ordered 14 <a href="/wiki/Territorial_authorities_of_New_Zealand" title="Territorial authorities of New Zealand">territorial authorities</a> to add fluoride to their water supplies. Bloomfield stated that this measure would boost the number of the New Zealand population receiving water fluoridation by from 51% to 60%.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-175"><a href="#cite_note-175">[175]</a></sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="South_America">South America</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_fluoridation_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=47" title="Edit section: South America">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Brazil">Brazil</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_fluoridation_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=48" title="Edit section: Brazil">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>By 2008, 41% of people (73.2 million) in Brazil were getting artificially-fluoridated water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-OIMextent0_24-12"><a href="#cite_note-OIMextent0-24">[24]</a></sup>
</p><p>Water fluoridation was first adopted in Brazil in the city of <a href="/wiki/Baixo_Guandu" title="Baixo Guandu">Baixo Guandu</a>, <a href="/wiki/Esp%C3%ADrito_Santo" title="Espírito Santo">ES</a>, in 1953.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-176"><a href="#cite_note-176">[176]</a></sup> A 1974 federal law required new or enlarged water treatment plants to have fluoridation, and its availability was greatly expanded in the 1980s, with optimum fluoridation levels set at 0.8 mg/L. Today, the expansion of fluoridation in Brazil is a governmental priority; Between 2005 and 2008, fluoridation became available to 7.6 million people in 503 <a href="/wiki/Municipalities_of_Brazil" title="Municipalities of Brazil">municipalities</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> As of 2008, 3,351 municipalities (60.6%) had adopted fluoridation, up from 2,466 in 2000.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-177"><a href="#cite_note-177">[177]</a></sup>
</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Chile">Chile</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_fluoridation_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=49" title="Edit section: Chile">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In <a href="/wiki/Chile" title="Chile">Chile</a> 70.5% of the population receives fluoridated water (10.1 million added by chemical means, 604,000 naturally occurring).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-178"><a href="#cite_note-178">[178]</a></sup> The <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Biobio_Region" title="Biobio Region">Biobio Region</a> is the only administrative division that doesn't fluoridate water.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-179"><a href="#cite_note-179">[179]</a></sup><sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Reliable_sources" title="Wikipedia:Reliable sources"><span title="The material near this tag may rely on an unreliable source. (April 2017)">unreliable source?</span></a></i>]</sup>
</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="References">References</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Water_fluoridation_by_country&amp;action=edit&amp;section=50" title="Edit section: References">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<li id="cite_note-WHO2011-5"><span class="mw-cite-backlink"><b><a href="#cite_ref-WHO2011_5-0">^</a></b></span> <span class="reference-text"><a class="external text" href="http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/44584/1/9789241548151_eng.pdf" rel="nofollow">Guidelines for Drinking-water Quality, 4th Edition</a> WHO, 2011. <link href="mw-data:TemplateStyles:r1133582631" rel="mw-deduplicated-inline-style"/><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/ISBN_(identifier)" title="ISBN (identifier)">ISBN</a> <a href="/wiki/Special:BookSources/9789241548151" title="Special:BookSources/9789241548151">9789241548151</a>. Page 168, 175, 372 and see also pp 370-73. See also J. Fawell, et al <a class="external text" href="http://apps.who.int/iris/bitstream/10665/43514/1/9241563192_eng.pdf?ua=1" rel="nofollow">Fluoride in Drinking-water</a>. WHO, 2006. Page 32. Quote: "Concentrations in drinking-water of about 1 mg l–1 are associated with a lower incidence of dental caries, particularly in children, whereas excess intake of fluoride can result in dental fluorosis. In severe cases this can result in erosion of enamel. The margin between the beneficial effects of fluoride and the occurrence of dental fluorosis is small and public health programmes seek to retain a suitable balance between the two"</span>
